More Than Fifty Trade Associations Petition for a Separate Qianzhuang Law 162

The city's Chinese medicine industry, iron industry, fruit and land goods industry, wood industry, Chinese grain and oil cake industry, rice store industry, advertising industry, biscuit candy canned food industry, seafood grocery industry, dried goods industry, paint industry, Chaozhou refined grocery industry, paper industry, color printing industry, camp factory industry, Chinese pigment industry, oil press factory industry, department store industry, knitting industry, transshipment customs clearance industry, kerosene industry, yarn and cotton weaving industry, antique industry, Chinese soap industry, etc., more than fifty trade associations jointly submitted a document to the Central Party Headquarters and the National Government yesterday, requesting the Legislative Yuan to expedite the enactment of a separate Qianzhuang Law, which stated: (Omitted above) I have read the news that Article 1 of the Banking Law passed by the Legislative Yuan stipulates that anyone who operates one of the following businesses but is not called a bank is also regarded as a bank, etc. Although the Qianzhuang is not explicitly listed in the article, it is actually included in it. Although the behavior of banks and Qianzhuang is similar on the surface, there is a big difference in their history and nature. The organization of banks belongs to a limited liability company, which has been in our country for a very short time. Even in remote towns, there is still no establishment of banks. The nature of their business is mostly buying and selling securities, managing real estate mortgages, and lending. The Qianzhuang industry is mostly a partnership nature. All shareholders bear unlimited liability. Its history in our country is very long. Even in inland cities, the Qianzhuang is the hub of finance. The nature of its business is to lend on credit as a common body. It is to put the two different natures into the same regulations, which is not appropriate. Moreover, when the domestic business is declining, the general small and medium-sized merchants rely on the Qianzhuang's credit to borrow money for turnover and circulation. If the Qianzhuang industry is forced to be restricted by the Banking Law, it will inevitably change its habit of lending on credit and take mortgaged goods as its goal. As a result, the Qianzhuang industry will be hindered by its business, and all industries will hinder its development. This is not the purpose of the government to love and protect industry and commerce. The law is responsible for adapting to the times. If it violates the times, why is it so valuable? The current environment in the country requires a Qianzhuang. It is not enough to adapt to the needs of the Chinese people unless a separate set of regulations is formulated. It is reasonable to submit a written application to your Ministry (Government) for consideration and transfer to the Legislative Yuan to speed up the deliberation and revision of the Qianzhuang Law to adapt to the times and meet the needs (omitted below).

The Silk and Satin Industry Association submitted a document to the Legislative Yuan yesterday, which stated: "Regarding the fact that the Banking Law is not applicable to the Qianzhuang industry, please enact a separate Qianzhuang law to suit the business conditions and avoid obstacles. I have read in the news that your hospital passed the Banking Law. I have carefully interpreted the meaning of the words in Article 1, which seems to include ordinary Qianzhuang in it. Therefore, the Qianzhuang Association in the city has had a quiet discussion about the obstacles to its business, and various businesses that have a relationship with the Qianzhuang also believe that the regulations cannot be suitable for the business conditions, and they all think that it is impossible. According to my country's commerce, all operations depend on the Qianzhuang's turnover to adjust the surplus and deficiency. It can pass through the youth and yellow and can be continued. It is the hub of all industries. From all cities and towns to various rural cities and towns, although the size is different, there is an organization of this industry. It has a long history in the business market and predates the production of the banking industry for thousands of years. If the organization is different, the nature is different, the advanced and the backward are forced into a kind of law, there must be a disease that does not conform to the people. It is only because the bank Qianzhuang, although the same as the financial industry, is completely different in nature. The bank is a limited company, and the Qianzhuang bears unlimited liability. The bank must mortgage loans, and the Qianzhuang can lend on credit. The mortgage of goods is sometimes poor, and the promotion of credit can be used at any time, so the Qianzhuang has a great impact on the flow of sales and the prosperity of the city. And the custom has been around for a long time, and all industries, large and small, are happy to deal with it. If there are dissimilar restrictions, it will not only be difficult for the Qianzhuang, but also the suffering of all industries. In the future, the operation will be stagnant, and the business market will decline, which will cause social panic. You are requested to enact a separate Qianzhuang law so that the customs can be dealt with and the financial center can be spared from changes, then the business is fortunate. There is also Article 5 of the same law, which states that the investor's property certificate must be attached when applying for approval. Although this method is for the sake of seriousness, to be fair, the content of the assets is often reluctant to be revealed. If the investors are worried about this, the entrepreneurial future will be reduced, and the social finance will be hindered. One heart of our association in all industries, so-called danger dare not keep silent, so the reason why the Banking Law does not apply to the Qianzhuang industry should be applied to the Qianzhuang industry. Please examine and approve to enact a separate Qianzhuang Law to suit the business conditions, which is for the public convenience.

Customs Clearance Industry Has Difficulty Resuming Work Temporarily 163

Cotton Cloth Association's Attitude Remains Firm

The Union Cannot Comply with the Order to Resume Work

The customs clearance workers' strike in the city has been instructed by the Social Affairs Bureau to resume work within a specified period. The transportation costs are still to be transferred by the cotton cloth industry to the union. The union decided at a meeting to resume the transportation of cotton cloth tomorrow. The cotton cloth industry expressed its opposition. The customs clearance union held a meeting yesterday to negotiate, but there was no result. Therefore, the union decided to postpone the resumption of transportation. The various situations are recorded separately below.

Meeting of the Cotton Cloth Association: After receiving instructions from the Social Affairs Bureau, Chairman Chen Songyuan of the Cotton Cloth Industry Association, in order to respect the instructions and seek a peaceful solution, specially convened an emergency meeting of the local cotton cloth industry at 2:00 PM yesterday. The representatives who attended the meeting still insisted that they would not stop until they achieved their goals. After Chairman Chen's repeated persuasion, they slightly eased their attitude. On the spot, they unanimously decided that they would refuse to deliver the matters and would not pay the passes unless the proposed conditions were agreed with the customs clearance union. They also publicly elected Chen Songyuan, Zhou Rong, Sun Shaozhong, and Shi Jiucheng as the responsible representatives to attend the customs clearance union meeting at the Shangbang Association.

Meeting of the Customs Clearance Union: The Customs Clearance Industry Union held a representative assembly at 3:00 PM yesterday. Shi Zhikun, You Senting, Xinchanglong, Zhu Wenchun, Huiji, Zhuo Jian, Ruiji, Wang Wenzhen, Xinchangyuan, Yan Yuanzhong, Yiyu, Jin Jiuxiang, Fuhe, Chen Zhongmo, Yonghe, Ni Wen, Guo Yihe, Yiyu Huang Zhihuan, Taikoo Yiyu Hu Ruyi, Yu Shungong, Zhou Jing, Dachuantong, Pan Mengyong, Renyi Gong, and Zheng Renye were present. Chen Songyuan, Zheng Zhonghe, Shi Jiucheng, Zhou Rong, Sun and other four people from the Cotton Cloth Association, Su Houxin and six people from the Customs Clearance Union were present. Chairman Shi Zhikun had a long discussion, but there was no specific solution to the conditions proposed by the Cotton Cloth Association.

General Assembly of the Customs Clearance Union: In order to comply with government orders, the Customs Clearance Union had decided to resume the customs clearance of cotton cloth, etc., starting tomorrow. Because the Cotton Cloth Association opposed it yesterday, it held an emergency representative assembly at 6:00 PM yesterday. Over 150 representatives from various industries, including Su Houxin, attended. Chairman He Yumin and recorder Yu Qishu. The chairman reported on the meeting of the Customs Clearance Union and decided that (1) the resumption of work will be postponed until the 20th, (2) a general assembly will be convened on the 19th, (3) if the cotton cloth industry is not sincere, cotton yarn and foreign goods will be stopped on Monday, (4) the inspection team will be restored and will immediately continue to go out for defense.

Cotton Cloth Industry Proposes Conditions: The Cotton Cloth Industry Association proposed five new conditions and requested the Transshipment Customs Clearance Industry Union to acknowledge them: (1) No matter which factory or warehouse the goods are in, the customs clearance workers should go to the factory to transport the goods by themselves. If there are still cases of refusal to push or transport the goods, the Customs Clearance Industry Union shall be fully responsible. (2) From Ning Shao New Warehouse in the south, Yangshupu Road in the northeast, and the warehouses along the river, Maigen Road in the west, Sanban Factory New Bridge, and the warehouses along the Suzhou River, and the ticket numbers and warehouses in the central area from the Bund in the east to Tibet Road in the west, from the Republic Road in the south to the Boundary Road in the north, the goods within this area should be transported by the customs clearance workers themselves without paying for transportation. (3) The transportation costs of the cotton cloth in this factory (a separate transportation cost table will be formulated) will be paid according to the table without special additions or demands. The settlement will be made once a week. The customs clearance union will first collect the transportation costs from the buyers. If the buyers refuse to pay, the cotton cloth industry and the customs clearance industry shall share the costs. (4) All other expenses such as pier donations, inspection fees, and stamp duty shall be collected by the customs clearance industry from the buyers and shall not involve the cotton cloth industry. (5) For goods in Pudong warehouses that are transported by foreign companies, they must be able to clear customs until 10:00 PM before they can be returned.

Coal Industry Association Plans to Solve Coal Supply Problems 164

Short-Term Solution - Recover Coal Debts According to Law

Long-Term Solution - Reclaim Coal Mines Held by Foreigners in China

The coal dispute resolution meeting at Kai Le still did not reach a solution yesterday. Various coal merchants are rushing to prepare a list of coal debts to be submitted to the Coal Industry Association, which will then forward it to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to request mediation from the Social Bureau in accordance with the law. The Coal Industry Association's opinions on the city's coal supply problem will be addressed in two steps: (1) Short-term measures: Recover the owed coal from the four distribution points according to the law; (2) Long-term measures: Since the Kai Le coal dispute arose from a shortage of coal supply, in addition to short-term measures, a fundamental solution to Shanghai's coal supply problem should be sought. Therefore, three proposals will be submitted to the National Assembly: (A) Reclaim the Kailuan Coal Mine: The joint venture contract between the Kailuan and Jizhou companies expired in 1920. Reclaiming it and operating it independently is justified in terms of law and reason, and there is no concern about a lack of capital for this profitable venture; (B) Extend the Cangshi Railway to Dagukou and connect it with the Zhengtai Railway. The tracks should be the same as the Zhengtai Railway to transport the massive amount of coal from Shanxi to supply the national needs and develop China's rich resources. Furthermore, connect the Ping Sui Railway from Kouhan to the vicinity of the Tongbao Coal Mine to facilitate the smooth transportation of Tongbao coal. Tongbao coal contains only one part per thousand of sulfur and can be considered the highest quality coal in the world, especially suitable for naval ships; (C) Reclaim the Fushun Coal Mine: The Fushun Coal Mine was forcibly occupied by Japanese troops and then transferred to the management of the South Manchuria Railway Company on April 1, 1907. It is now declared that it should be reclaimed and operated independently in accordance with the law. The above two short-term measures are awaiting mediation by the Social Bureau, and the long-term measures are currently being drafted and will be submitted to the National Assembly for discussion.

Rong Zongjing's Speech at the Industrial and Commercial Management Association 166

Strategies to Rescue the Textile and Flour Industries

The China Industrial and Commercial Management Association held its sixth luncheon discussion meeting at the Lianhua General Association yesterday afternoon. Director Dr. Kong Yongzhi specially came to Shanghai from Beijing to chair the meeting. Attendees included Directors Rong Zongjing, Wu Qingtai, Guo Bingwen, Qian Chengxu, Shi Youming, Shou Yicheng, Tao Leqin, Xu Chao, Xu Dinglan, Zhang Xianglin, Zhu Yinong, Zhao Shutong, Cao Yunxiang, and other members. After the meal, Chairman Rong Zongjing, Director, gave a speech on the difficulties in operating China's textile and flour industries and the strategies to rescue them, stating that the textile and flour industries are of great importance to China's social economy. In recent years, competition with countries such as Britain, Japan, and Canada has become increasingly fierce, and the difficulties have been immense. The main reasons are excessive tax burdens, traffic obstruction, high freight costs, poor raw material quality, and unscientific factory management. The key to saving the situation lies in improving cotton production, reducing taxes and freight costs, and implementing scientific management. He also stated that Japanese flour can be imported duty-free in Dalian, Andong, and other places, encroaching on the market in the Eastern Provinces, which puts Chinese producers at a disadvantage. He hopes that the government authorities will find ways to help. Furthermore, China has too few textile experts, and he hopes that domestic engineering universities will establish textile specialties to train specialized talents. Chairman Kong expressed his gratitude on behalf of the association and stated that Premier Sun advocated that psychological construction and material construction should be given equal importance. Although China's industrial construction faces difficulties, as long as the whole country works together and all industry leaders can effectively promote scientific management, the future is still bright. Subsequently, Director Shou Yicheng of the association distributed a copy of the book "German Commercial Warfare Strategies" translated by Secretary-General Cao Yunxiang, which is very helpful for Chinese entrepreneurs, to the members present at the meeting. They were all eager to read it.

Goods Displayed at the Exhibition Hall to be Returned 167

Limited to Clearing Out by the End of May

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Commodity Exhibition Hall of this city found that the items sent for display by various factories were too old and dilapidated. They have been returned and stored in the warehouse. If this continues, the items will inevitably be moldy and damaged, which is a pity. The hall is now preparing for the Double Tenth Festival's Tenth Anniversary Exhibition and the Permanent National Goods Commercial Exhibition and has started to clear out the old items in the warehouse. The goods must be cleared out completely before the end of May this year. Separate letters have been sent to the factories, instructing them to send personnel to the hall on a specific date to take back the old items to complete the procedures. If they fail to take them back after the deadline, the hall will sell all the items at a low price to close the matter.

"Piggy" Ah Mei Executed 168

Executed in Xincang the Day Before Yesterday

Taihu Gang's famous bandit leader, Taibao A She, Xu Tianxiong, and his younger brother, Xu Fusheng, were ordered to be executed in Zhangyan Town, Jinshan County, on the 16th, as reported earlier. His subordinate bandit, "Piggy" Ah Mei, Wang Qiming, was ordered to be escorted to Xincang Town, Pinghu County, for execution on the 17th. According to a report from Pinghu, "Piggy" Ah Mei committed more than a thousand crimes in the vicinity of Pinghu. Therefore, the Songjiang Bandit Suppression Headquarters requested and was approved to execute him. Yesterday (the 17th), Cao Pang, the bandit suppression commander of the four counties of Jinshan, Songjiang, Jiading, and Qingpu, and Xu Pucheng, the district chief of the first district of the Jiangsu Water Police Force, led dozens of soldiers and police officers on warships and escorted the bandit leader to Xincang in the afternoon. He was immediately tied up and beheaded at Xinjia Bridge in Zhujia Alley and his head displayed to the public. It took two strikes to sever his head from his body. The bandit's attitude remained the same as before his execution. Thousands of spectators gathered. The bandit's head has been taken away by the army and placed in a wooden cage to be displayed in the areas where he committed crimes.

Location of the Sunken Dachang Steamer 169

Customs Installs Buoy to Mark the Sunken Ship

Customs Maritime Affairs Section Patrol Engineering Division Bulletin No. 1002: This patrol engineering division, upon investigation by the Jianghai Customs Tax Office, found that a steamer sank in the Changjiang (Yangtze) River channel within its jurisdiction and installed a buoy to mark the sunken ship. The situation and position are listed below: Because the Dachang steamer sank in the Changjiang (Yangtze) River channel, its location is 85 degrees and 10 minutes west of the Wusong Lighthouse, 3.8 nautical miles away. The entire ship is not visible on the surface. A green buoy is installed, flashing a green light once every three seconds, that is, on for 0.3 seconds and off for 2.7 seconds. The buoy is moored 15% of a mile away from the sunken ship at 88 degrees east of south. From the buoy, the Wusong Lighthouse is 85 degrees and 6 minutes west of north, 3.96 nautical miles away. The above degrees are all based on the compass direction and refer to the Chinese Navy Hydrographic Chart No. 1011. All ships should pay attention and remember this to avoid accidents. This is a notice from the Patrol Engineering Division, Xi Liman, April 16, 1931.

Resolution of the Gonghe Steamer New and Old Workers Dispute 170

Results of the Arbitration by the Wuhan Municipal Government

The Gonghe Steamer of the Qiahe Company had a dispute over labor between new and old workers, which was mediated by the Social Bureau and the Municipal Party Department of both Shanghai and Wuhan, but to no avail. The Ministry of Industry and Commerce designated the Wuhan Municipal Government as the competent administrative authority for the case and granted it arbitration powers, as detailed in previous reports in this newspaper. It is now known that the ship arrived in Wuhan on the 14th. The next day, the Municipal Government convened an arbitration meeting. The attendees included Ren Yaoxian from the Municipal Government, Gao Lang from the Municipal Party Department, Zhou Xingbin from the Local Court, Zhou Yunduan from the General Chamber of Commerce, Jiang Huanruo from the Labor Union, Ma Xisan and others representing the new workers, Huang Wenchen and Chen Bonian representing the Seamen's Union, and Xu Bingxiang representing the comprador. Chairman Ren Yaoxian, in addition to having representatives from all parties report on the situation, decided on the following: The 80 old workers will continue to work as usual. 30 of the 38 new workers will be allowed to stay, and who goes and who stays will be decided by drawing lots. Before the 8 workers who are laid off find other jobs, the new workers will subsidize them for a period of four months, and the amount will be determined by the new workers themselves. Regarding the issue of the 30 new workers joining the union, the Party Department and the Municipal Government will jointly send a letter to the Seamen's General Union to approve their membership to provide protection. Before the new workers join the union, Chen, the comprador, should pay a deposit, but the amount should not exceed the original amount. Once the membership formalities are completed, the comprador will return the deposit in full to the new workers to achieve unity and show equality. All three parties had no objection and signed on the spot. Thus, the labor dispute that had been dragging on for more than a year came to an end. The ship is expected to arrive in Shanghai this morning, and it is said that when it sails to Wuhan the day after tomorrow, the 30 new workers can resume their work on board.

Yesterday's Negotiations on Compensation for the Victims of the Yangtze River Steamer Disaster 171

Social Bureau Sends Personnel to Investigate

No Results in Negotiations

The Changjiang Steamer, which is operated by the Shanghai Steamboat Company as an agent, ran aground and sank in the waters off Wenzhou in the middle of last month, drowning many people. The surviving crew members, who reside in this city, have repeatedly demanded compensation from the company for losses and for the families of the deceased. Initially, the company only agreed to compensate each of the deceased with 200 yuan and each of the survivors with 50 yuan. After serious negotiations by the Seamen's General Union, the company agreed to compensate each of the deceased with 325 yuan and each of the survivors with 65 yuan. The crew members did not accept this. Yesterday afternoon at 2:00 p.m., negotiations resumed between Li Zuyao, representing the Seamen's General Union, Ling Hong and Lin Xiong, representing the surviving crew members, and Cai Jingbo and Kang Shenji, representing the company, and others, at the Shanghai Steamboat Company at 35 Renji Road. Zhu Guilin, an official from the third section of the Social Bureau, also went to investigate. The workers' representatives put forward five demands: (1) Compensation for the deceased should follow the precedent of the Xinchang and Xinhua steamers, at least 500 yuan per person; (2) Survivors should be compensated at least 150 yuan per person; (3) Reimbursement of 250 yuan for the cost of food and lodging for the survivors in Shanghai; (4) Wages should be paid from April 1 until the crew members return to Hong Kong; (5) Reimbursement of travel expenses for each person to return to Hong Kong. The company representatives said that these demands had to be telegraphed to the Hai Fang General Company for approval before they could be accepted, so there were no results.

All Silkworm Moth Workers Went on Strike Yesterday 172

Thirty-Six Factories Participating in the Strike

Hope for Resumption of Work Today

The silkworm moth workers in this city went on strike yesterday because the company violated the conditions for increasing wages, and they did not attend the talks convened by the authorities. The labor union announced that if the company did not pay the arrears by the 17th, they would go on strike. Thirty-six factories joined the strike. The Social Bureau obtained the company representatives' permission to fulfill the conditions and ordered the workers to resume work immediately, so there is hope for a resumption of work today. The situation yesterday is detailed below:

Reasons for the Strike: Article 2 of the conditions agreed upon between the Silkworm Moth Workers Union and the company on October 28 last year stated that the factory would increase the wages of workers by 2 yuan per month, with the amount to be determined by the factory. The implementation period would be when more than half of the silk factories in Shanghai resumed operation. The silkworm moth workers requested the Social Bureau in March to order the company to fulfill the conditions because 80% of the silk factories in the city had resumed operation. The bureau summoned them three times for questioning, but the company did not send representatives, considering that they had no sincerity in the negotiations. Therefore, they all went on strike yesterday morning.

Number of Factories Joining: The silkworm moth workers joined the strike at the following factories: Toubei Gonggu Dou, Tanjiachiao Guangdechang, Zhicheng, Xin, Changda, Lunjuncheng, Juxing, Yuan, Yu San, De Tai, Wanchang, Hefeng, Yuncheng, Buxiang, Yunchang, Yuancheng, Jucheng, Yunfeng, Yingfeng, Wanfeng, Ruihe, Houyu, Dechang, Xiexingji, Xielong, Tongyi, Jin Wuji, Huichang, Xie Mao, Longxiang, Tongyi, Dexin, Tiancheng, Xiexinggong, Jingcheng, Wufeng, etc., totaling thirty-six factories.

Authorities Intervene: The Municipal Social Bureau learned that the silkworm moth workers had gone on strike due to the wage increase issue and immediately sent Guo Yongxi to investigate the truth and mediate. Zhu Zirong, the company representative, believed that the silkworm moth industry was different from other industries and that once a strike occurred, the stored cocoons would inevitably be useless. Therefore, he went to the Social Bureau last night and promised to take full responsibility for persuading the factories to immediately fulfill the conditions, but hoped for an immediate resumption of work. The bureau immediately ordered the silkworm moth workers to resume work immediately after receiving the report.

Union Petition: The Silkworm Moth Workers Union submitted a petition to the Social Bureau yesterday requesting a remedy, stating that the company had deceived the weak workers and refused to fulfill the legal labor-capital treatment contract, which had now sparked a labor unrest and left them helpless. They requested a review and compliance. The union stated that the workers were suffering from difficult living conditions and signed a labor-capital treatment contract, but the company intentionally deceived and delayed its implementation until now. After discussion, they submitted a request to the bureau for review and had been summoned to the bureau several times for questioning. However, the company was ignorant and disregarded the superiors and treated the workers like horses and cattle. Now the workers are oppressed and unable to extricate themselves. They unanimously took a rest today and appealed for the righteous to help. The union believes that this labor unrest was caused by excessive oppression by the company, which is to blame and cannot shirk its responsibility. The union is unable to remedy the urgent situation, so it has prepared a document and respectfully requests the bureau to review and comply. Submitted to the Shanghai Municipal Social Bureau.

Further News on the Japanese Ship Colliding with a Civilian Ship 175

The Japanese ship, Yijin Maru of the Dalian Steamship Company, collided with the moored civilian ship Xu Yuanjie at Renjiagang, Nantong, at about 8:00 p.m. on the 10th of this month due to a mistake in the course. Because the Japanese ship did not provide assistance in accordance with maritime law at the time and because it was heavily loaded with ballast stones, the ship sank and could not be salvaged. The rising and falling tides gradually shifted the ship to deeper waters, making it more difficult to handle. The Yijin Maru, which caused the accident, had the shipowner, Ling Jiang, sign a document acknowledging the collision and agreeing to resolve it in Shanghai. However, when the victim ship arrived in Shanghai, the ship had already sailed to Qingdao with cargo. When they contacted its business organization, the Dalian Steamboat Company, they refused to compensate. They have requested the Zhejiang Shipping Association to send personnel to negotiate and have sent letters to the Municipal Party Department, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, and other groups to request assistance in urging them to quickly realize their mistake and compensate for the loss. Local News

Disposition of Communist Development Company Assets to Solicit Creditor Consent 177

Resolution Achieved Through Mediation by Pan Gongzhan Yesterday Afternoon

Chinese and Western Pharmacy to be Unsealed Tomorrow

The Japanese and Chinese Bank case caused a dispute due to inconsistent opinions among the creditor groups. Social Bureau Director Pan Gongzhan mediated to quickly resolve this issue. Yesterday afternoon, he specially convened representatives of various creditors, lawyers, and the accountants of Pan and Wu, who were handling the liquidation, at the Municipal Government's Recreation Club on Weihaiwei Road. Attendees included Municipal Government Secretary-General Yu Hongjun, Wu Jingxiong, Jiang Yiping, Chen Tingrui, Dong Yu, Yan Luqing, Bian Jialu, and other lawyers, and the accountants of Pan and Wu. Chairman Pan Gongzhan first had lawyer Jiang Yiping, representing the four voluntary lawyers appointed by the Social Bureau, state the process of applying to the Special District Court for the pre-trial attachment of the assets of the Communist Development Company and the reasons why the pre-trial attachment had to be implemented. He then stated that the revocation of the pre-trial attachment required the condition that the creditors represented by the four lawyers should have the right to agree on the disposition of the assets of the Communist Development Company and Huang Chujiu. He repeatedly stated the necessity of the creditors having the right to agree. The reasons were sufficient. After detailed discussion, a compromise was proposed. It was recognized that the creditor group had the right to agree to the disposition of the assets, but because there were too many creditors, it was too cumbersome to obtain the consent of each one. The representative lawyers of the creditor group should be responsible for contacting the accountants of Wu and Pan. The accountants of Wu and Pan also had no objection. Finally, two resolutions were passed: (1) When the accountants undertaking the liquidation dispose of all the assets of the Communist Development Company, such as the Zhaopan of the Chinese and Western Pharmacy, they should first formulate a plan and convene a meeting of all representative lawyers of the creditors three days in advance to discuss it. After obtaining the consent of the majority of the lawyers present at the meeting, they should report it to the French Concession for a decision; (2) The four lawyers, including Wu Jingxiong, should explain the whole story of the case to the parties concerned and request the Special District Local Court to revoke the pre-trial attachment of the Chinese and Western Pharmacy, etc., and the accountants should manage the accounts of the various business institutions of the Communist Development Company to provide protection. The Social Bureau has notified the accountants of Wu and Pan and the lawyers of these two resolutions, and all dispositions of the assets of the Communist Development Company must be in accordance with these resolutions. Therefore, the dispute over the right to agree has come to an end, and the progress of the case is expected to be smooth. It is also reported that the four lawyers, including Wu Jingxiong, have drafted a petition to the Special District Court to revoke the pre-trial attachment and plan to submit it on the morning of the 20th. The Chinese and Western Pharmacy is expected to be unsealed on the 20th. For the convenience of the proceedings, the four lawyers have opened a separate room in the law firm of Jiang Yiping at 48 Sichuan Road as an office for the case to handle all matters.

The Jihong Temple's Jigong Hall was Burned Down 178

Worker Flicked a Candle Wick, Causing the Disaster

Hall of Stars and Jigong Hall Destroyed

The Jigong Hall of the Longhua Temple was suddenly burned down yesterday morning. The details are as follows: The abbot of the temple, Yuanzhao, recently hired many workers to repair the walls and clean the Buddha statues in various rooms in preparation for the incense burning season. The workers lived upstairs in the north second room of the west hall in the second courtyard, and the floor below was the Hall of Stars. Straw mats were laid for the beds. They worked from 6:00 a.m. to 6:00 p.m. every day. At 4:30 a.m. yesterday, the workers had all gotten up, but it was still dark. A candle lamp was lit in the room. A worker named Wang Daoming saw that the candle wick was too long and the light was dim, so he flicked off the candle wick with his finger and left it on the floor. He did not expect that the candle wick would fall into the straw and ignite it. At that time, the workers did not notice it. After a while, they suddenly heard the sound of the fish gong. The workers all went downstairs for breakfast and locked the door of the room. At 7:30 a.m., they saw smoke filling the room upstairs, and the fire had already spread. In an instant, the roof was on fire. The Longhua branch of the sixth district, third section, was nearby. Patrol officer Qiu Pengfei learned of the fire and immediately led all the police officers to help put out the fire. He also used the telephone to notify the fire departments of each district to come to the scene to put out the fire. However, the wind was too strong and it was impossible to control it for a while. Moreover, there was no tap water, so they had to use river water to put out the fire. It was not extinguished until 8:25 a.m. The Hall of Stars and two buildings and the Jigong Hall and three rooms were burned down. The abbot of the temple, Yuanzhao, sent the worker who caused the fire, Wang Daoming, to the police station for investigation. Director Liu briefly questioned him, and according to his confession, he was a 49-year-old man from Ningbo. He confessed the above and sent a document to the bureau for verification.

The Gang of Bandits Who Murdered While Smuggling on the Dianshan Lake Were All Sentenced to Death 179

The bandits Xue Wu, also known as Xue Zhiming, Yang Yin San, and Xue Guo Qing, etc., previously robbed a stone boat in Dianshan Lake, sank the owner, Zhong Hehua, to the bottom of the lake to his death, and sold all the goods on the boat for money. They also raped the owner's wife, Cui Hu, and then sold her to Li Da Jinzi. This case was not discovered in Shanghai until February of last year. Xue Wu, Yang Yin San, and Xue Guo Qing were all arrested by the Public Security Bureau. Tang Er and Guo Wei Long were also arrested and sent to the Local Court. After the court prosecutor and criminal court judge conducted a detailed investigation and review of the evidence for seventeen months, it was finally found that Xue Wu, Yang Yin San, and Xue Guo Qing were the main perpetrators. It was found that the criminals' crime details and methods were cruel and their crimes were extremely deep. If they were not sentenced to the most severe punishment, it would not be enough to atone for their crimes. Therefore, after the debate was over, Judge Zhao Yongzhou opened the court at 3:00 p.m. yesterday to announce the verdict. The three defendants, Xue Wu, also known as Xue Zhiming, Yang Yin San, and Xue Guo Qing, were sentenced to death for the crime of robbery and murder, and sentenced to eight years of imprisonment for the crime of raping and abducting women, to be executed together with the death penalty and deprived of civil rights for life. The remaining Li Da Jinzi, Feng Lian Bao, Tang Er, and Guo Wei Long were all acquitted. After the judgment was completed, the three criminals, Xue Wu, etc., were sent to the detention center for imprisonment pending review and execution by the province.

A Mother-Son Lawsuit 180

Mother Wants to Dissolve Relationship with Son

Evidence Insufficient, Judgment Dismissed

The local woman Hou Chen has been a widow for many years and has one son and one daughter, who are all adults. Her daughter is married and her son, Gui Sheng, is married to a woman named Xu. However, after she married into the family, the sisters-in-law began to argue, and then the mother-son and mother-in-law and daughter-in-law had opinions from time to time, and the good family became a place of disputes. Recently, Hou Chen sued the Special District Local Court, claiming that Gui Sheng was adopted and not her biological son, and requested to dissolve the mother-son and mother-in-law-daughter-in-law relationship. Gui Sheng hired lawyer Hong Shihhao to defend him, denying that he was adopted and claiming that Hou Chen gambled away her family property, borrowed money from Indians to make a living, and had a son and recruited a son-in-law, which was against the law. He requested that it be corrected. The court opened the trial a few days ago and summoned Hou Chen to testify. Hou Chen said that she only gave birth to one daughter, and because she had no son, she adopted Gui Sheng as her son, educated him when he was young, and married a wife for him when he grew up. Since their marriage, the son and daughter-in-law have been uneasy at home, colluding with each other, making excuses to quarrel, and even wielding knives and disregarding their elders. Now that they have separated, she should be allowed to dissolve the relationship with them. Lawyer Huang, representing the plaintiff, submitted an adoption document and called Shen Fusheng as a witness. Lawyer Hong Shihhao, defending the defendant, said that there should be considerable evidence to support the adoption claim before it could be believed. The adoption document was from 1907, and the witnesses in it were all dead, making it difficult to distinguish the truth from falsehood. Shen Fusheng was the son of the plaintiff, so it was difficult to testify. As for the separation of mother-son and mother-in-law and daughter-in-law, it is a common trend in modern times, and it is also a helpless measure for the son. It is not acceptable in terms of etiquette, but it is still understandable in terms of sentiment. However, kinship cannot be broken due to separation. The defendant did not know who gave birth to him when he was born, but before the plaintiff provides conclusive evidence, he should be considered a biological son and is willing to undergo procedures such as blood dripping to clarify the truth. Yesterday, the court ruled to dismiss the plaintiff's lawsuit, and the plaintiff was responsible for the litigation costs. The reason was that the witnesses in the adoption document were no longer alive, making it difficult to distinguish the truth from falsehood, and other evidence was also difficult to rely on. Therefore, the plaintiff lost the case.

Embezzlement Case of the Day and Night Bank Staff 183

Continued Trial at the French Concession Court Yesterday

Huang Xianzong Awaited to Testify

Chen Zhiquan, the manager of the Shanghai Day and Night Bank and chief accountant of the Gongfa Company, along with Chen Yuqing and Chen Xunqing, both in the accounting department, were accused of embezzlement by Pan Zhaobang and Wu Zheng, the liquidators of the Day and Night Bank, in the French Concession Court. The court ordered officials to arrest and detain Chen Zhiquan and Chen Yuqing at the police station, awaiting investigation. This information has already been reported in the newspaper. Yesterday at 10:00 AM, the French Concession Court convened a hearing. Lawyers Fei Xizhen and Yan Luqing, representing various creditors, were present in court. First, the two accountants, Pan and Wu, stated that after the Day and Night Bank collapsed, the court appointed them as liquidators. The defendants provided six account books. After examining these books, the accountants found that the appearance of the books was unusually new and the accounts within were inconsistent. Therefore, they requested the detention of the defendants. Later, after receiving official capital account books and comparing them with the books submitted by the defendants, the accountants found a significant difference in the age of the books, further indicating collusion, fraud, and forgery on the part of the defendants. It was also discovered that on the day of Huang Chu Jiu's death, the 19th, the Day and Night Bank paid out over 2 million yuan. There were also five checks issued by Huang Chu Jiu totaling over 1 million yuan. Although they bore Huang Chu Jiu's personal seal, the signature was not Huang Chu Jiu's. According to the bank's articles of association, withdrawals require either a signature, a seal, or both, with the official seal as the standard. However, the withdrawals made by Huang Chu Jiu relied solely on the seal, and the signature was not his own. As the bank manager, how could the defendant not notice this and authorize the payment? Defendant Chen Zhiquan testified that Huang Chu Jiu, due to illness, instructed his son, Huang Xianzong, to come and withdraw the funds, and the signature was also made by Xianzong on his behalf because Huang Chu Jiu was the general manager. Accountant Pan also stated that Huang Chu Jiu mortgaged eight title deeds to the Day and Night Bank, valued at 800,500 yuan. The defendant then remortgaged the title deeds to the Siming Bank and the China Industrial Bank in the name of the Day and Night Bank for 680,000 yuan, a difference of over 100,000 yuan. This not only caused losses to the Day and Night Bank but also harmed the creditors. Subsequently, the defendant's representative, lawyer Yao Zhaodi, made a defense. Judge Zhu then ordered the defendants to be remanded in custody and adjourned the hearing for seven days, summoning Huang Xianzong to testify and conduct further investigation.

The Great Northern Telegraph Company's 60th Anniversary 187

A look at the past and present development of submarine telegraph cables

The *Shanghai Evening Post and Mercury* reports that the Great Northern Telegraph Company has been laying submarine telegraph cables along the Chinese coast for 60 years. Today (the 18th) marks its 60th anniversary. The company laid a cable from Hong Kong to Shanghai in 1871 and then from Shanghai to Nagasaki in the same year. The following year, it directly connected to Europe. The company was initially established on Nanjing Road under the name "Great Northern Telegraph Company." The Hong Kong-Shanghai line was inaugurated on this day sixty years ago. On the first day, only seventy messages were sent, which cannot be compared to the current volume.

New Discovery in Chemical Therapy for Tuberculosis

Dr. Koch Discovers the Pathogen of Tuberculosis

Dr. Bergell Successfully Develops a Method for Dewaxing Tubercle Bacilli

The Pathogen of Tuberculosis 189

Exactly forty-nine years ago, on March 24, 1882, Dr. Robert Koch, a German medical saint, presented a highly valuable medical paper at the Physiology Congress in Berlin, Germany, titled "The Cause of Tuberculosis." The purpose of the doctor's report was to state that tuberculosis (i.e., consumption) is a specific infectious disease, not a hereditary disease, and he cited various examples to prove it (such as the culture, staining, and animal experiments of tubercle bacilli). This opened a special and unique chapter in the history of tuberculosis research over the past three thousand years. With the pathogen of tuberculosis identified, a definitive standard was established for diagnosing tuberculosis.

Tubercle bacilli are microscopic fungi. Their shape is extremely small and minute. If one "gram" of it is weighed, the number would be more than 3.5 billion. Their reproductive capacity is astonishing, destroying human tissue and causing the most terrible tuberculous diseases. When these bacteria are discharged from the human body, they cannot reproduce at all and can only maintain their survival. However, once they have the opportunity to invade the human body, they occupy the delicate lungs and establish a base of operations, unleashing their terrible power. Alas, the greatest enemy of mankind is tuberculosis, which is to be feared.

The Structure of Tubercle Bacilli 190

In the past, most doctors, not understanding the unique structure of tubercle bacilli, believed that all bacteria could be eradicated with disinfectant drugs, administered internally or by injection, just like "606" for syphilis. After Dr. Bergell's painstaking research, he announced that tubercle bacilli have a special defense mechanism that can resist attacks from all external drugs. The tubercle bacillus is composed of an inner membrane of neutral fat and an outer membrane of acid-fast wax. Unless a method is found to break through the wax barrier and dissolve the fatty armor, it is impossible to capture and destroy the tubercle bacilli. Moreover, when tubercle bacilli invade a local part of the human body, they erode the surrounding area and form a stubborn nodule that blocks blood flow, preventing generally injected or ingested disinfectant drugs from penetrating even a single step beyond the restricted area. It is like a specially guarded zone, and the drug's power cannot reach the affected area. Therefore, even if the entire body is immersed in a pool of drugs, it cannot harm a single hair of the tubercle bacilli. Therefore, the only battle strategy for eradicating tubercle bacilli must meet at least the following two preconditions:

(1) The drug must be able to break through the nodules and reach the affected area directly.

(2) It must also be able to strip away or dissolve the waxy and fatty inner and outer membranes.

Only in this way can the effect of breaking through barriers and capturing the enemy be achieved. Otherwise, it is like scratching an itch from outside a shoe. The tubercle bacilli, under these two layers of protection, secretly laugh at human helplessness.

Dr. Koch, the German medical saint and discoverer of tubercle bacilli

Successful Dewaxing of Tubercle Bacilli 191

Since Dr. Koch discovered tubercle bacilli as the cause of tuberculosis (i.e., consumption), scholars of tuberculosis from the East and West have striven to research and develop a magic formula to kill these bacteria. However, their efforts have all failed because they did not understand the profound theory that tubercle bacilli secrete a waxy substance to surround their bodies to defend against external forces. For example, Hammarsten-Harris and others discovered that the application of 5% to 10% caustic potash solution could remove the acid-fast wax of tubercle bacilli. Later, Morquin used chlorine gas to remove the acid-fast wax. However, this dewaxing method can only be applied to staining methods for microscopic examination. The drug's properties are too toxic for practical use on the human body.

In recent years, occasional successful results have been achieved by applying chaulmoogra oil to leprosy. Leprosy bacilli and tubercle bacilli are both acid-fast bacteria of the same nature, and chaulmoogra oil has a dewaxing effect and a bactericidal power a hundred times greater than carbolic acid. This aroused widespread attention among scholars, who tried to apply chaulmoogra oil to tuberculosis patients, hoping to achieve results. They used various chemical methods to extract the main components of chaulmoogra oil and tested them on tuberculosis patients, hoping to achieve a corresponding effect. However, this was only effective for skin and superficial tuberculosis, and it still could not achieve any effect on deep organ tuberculosis, such as the lungs, liver, and kidneys.

Therefore, Dr. Bergell, the great teacher of all tuberculosis patients in the world, went a step further, collecting various medicinal substances of animal, plant, and mineral origin, and painstakingly researching them, hoping to find a dewaxing agent that was peaceful and non-toxic. For decades, he tirelessly devoted all his efforts and energy to seeking the most rational and effective chemical agent. Finally, he discovered that a certain effective component in the pressed juice of the intestinal mesenteric gland of a special animal has a strong dewaxing effect on tubercle bacilli. He immediately applied this component to tubercle bacilli, and the result was complete dewaxing. Since then, the long-held view of doctors in the East and West that artificial removal of the acid-fast properties of tubercle bacilli was impossible has been completely overturned. This is truly a new dawn in the treatment of tuberculosis, a major question in the medical world for thousands of years.

Chemical Therapy for Tuberculosis 192

The cause of tuberculosis (i.e., consumption) is tubercle bacilli. Once these bacteria enter the human body, they form nodules in the affected area to block blood flow. Tubercle bacilli can also secrete an acid-fast wax to surround their bodies and defend against invasion by all external drugs. Therefore, although various bactericidal drugs are taken internally or injected, they cannot reach the actual body of the bacteria. The natural therapy, symptomatic therapy, physical therapy, serum therapy, drug therapy, and other therapies commonly used by doctors in the past have not been completely successful, and the saying that there is no cure for consumption is widespread because this profound theory was not known. Based on the above theory, modern tuberculosis scholars continue to research tirelessly, and the result is the creation of this chemical holy agent for killing all tuberculosis bacteria, called Sanosln. This drug was successfully invented based on the latest medical theories of Dr. Koch, the German discoverer of tubercle bacilli, and Dr. Bergell, the German inventor of tubercle bacilli dewaxing. According to experimental reports from various tuberculosis sanatoriums in Germany, Switzerland, and other countries, this drug has the effect of penetrating the nodules of tuberculous lesions and dissolving the wax, and it also has bactericidal power. It can radically cure stage one, two, and three tuberculosis and has a proven effect in all cases. In China, it has been tested by the Central Health Laboratory of the National Government, and the drug's properties are peaceful and non-toxic, with no side effects. A brief description of the therapeutic effects is given below:

(1) When the power of "Sanosln" is tested in a test tube, tubercle bacilli lose their acid-fast properties after one minute, and after three minutes, the tubercle bacilli are completely killed, with none spared.

(2) Animal experiments have found that "Sanosln" can penetrate into tuberculous lesions. Examination of the latent tubercle bacilli in the lesions shows that they have all lost their acid-fast properties, proving that the wax has been completely dissolved.

(3) If the patient takes "Sanosln" for about a week, they will see good results such as sputum dilution and a decrease in body temperature.

(4) If they continue to take "Sanosln" for more than thirty to sixty days, they will see an increase in weight, an increase in appetite, and all symptoms gradually alleviating, thus achieving the great effect of bringing them back to life.

Dissection of Bandit Corpses Not Allowed 196

Tongde Hospital Wanted to Use Them for Academic Research

The District Court Prohibited Further Desecration Due to Difficulty in Executing Sentences

The other day, the District Court executed the four bandits, Yang Zhengting and others, sentenced by the Special District Court at the Second Prison in Caohejing. After the execution, the corpses were ordered to be collected by the Tang Guild Hall, awaiting relatives to claim them. However, Tongde Hospital in the Public Concession took away the corpses of the executed criminals Yang Zhengting and Li Kepeng for dissection and experimentation. This was discovered by the District Court Prosecutor yesterday morning. Since the criminals had relatives who would claim the corpses in the future, and since they had already been sentenced to death by shooting for their crimes, their corpses should not be further desecrated. Furthermore, desecration of corpses is prohibited by law and unacceptable to morality. The court cannot act illegally, so it immediately notified the hospital to not allow the dissection and ordered them to return the corpses to the prison for collection to show respect for humanity.

Ring the Doorbell Before Buying Opium 197

The Method is Very Appropriate

Police Handle the Matter According to the Law

Xia Chen, a woman who has recently been selling opium, has a doorbell installed on the front door of her residence at 19 Wuzhou Road. Anyone who wants to buy opium must first ring the doorbell and then go to the back door of the house. She will then open the back door and let them in. Those who do not know this secret will not be able to buy it. Recently, someone revealed this secret to the police, who sent a detective to purchase two small bags of opium. On the afternoon of the other day, at 2:00 PM, the police chief led the detectives to make an arrest, first ringing the doorbell at the front door and then going to the back door. The second landlord of the house, Ge Wang, was already waiting at the back door and was arrested. They then entered the house and arrested Xia Chen, searching her residence and finding twenty-two small bags of opium, a set of opium paraphernalia, and cash, including two silver coins that the police chief recognized as the ones he had sent someone to buy opium with earlier. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Special District Court. Judge Feng Shide conducted a preliminary hearing and, finding the evidence sufficient, immediately sentenced Xia Chen to one year and four months of imprisonment and a fine of 320 yuan. Ge Wang was sentenced to six months of imprisonment, and the opium was confiscated.

A Ferry in Pudong Collided 199

Passengers and Family Members Drowned

The Pudong ferry operated by Jiang Kunhua departed from Shanghai the other day. Ling Qingtang, the owner of a construction company, and his wife and children, a total of six or seven people, chartered Jiang's boat to visit graves in the countryside of Datuan Township. The boat also carried cargo such as sugar, northern goods, and tung oil. It departed during high tide the other night and arrived near Xinchang at about 4:00 AM yesterday. It was still dark when they suddenly heard the whistle of a steamer approaching rapidly. Seeing that the steamer was traveling quickly, Jiang steered the boat towards the dock and shouted to slow down the steamer. However, the steamer still approached rapidly and crashed into Jiang's boat head-on. The hull was shattered, and the tide rushed into the boat. The passengers, including Ling Qingtang, were shocked by the crash and the water rushing into the front of the boat. They came out of the cabin and shouted for help, while Ling's wife and daughter cried out. Seeing the accident, the steamer stopped and rescued the people, towing Jiang's boat to the dock. Ling and his wife and children were rescued to the steamer. However, Ling's wife and daughter were extremely panicked and accidentally fell into the river. It was not known at the time. When Ling was rescued to the steamer and checked, he did not see his wife and daughter. He immediately asked the steamer to search for them. It was dark at the time, making the search difficult. They had not been found by daybreak. The steamer that caused the accident belongs to Shen, the owner of a Pudong kiln. Because Shen had important business in Shanghai, Shen sat on the ship and started to Shen at two o'clock yesterday morning. After the accident, Ling negotiated with the steamer about the loss of the boat. Shen comforted Ling, saying that it was the error of the steamer's helmsman and was willing to be responsible for salvaging Ling's wife and daughter's corpses and all the losses in the boat. Ling initially refused, but Shen repeatedly persuaded him and eventually agreed.

Xie Mingwan Assassinated 200

Stabbed Seven or Eight Times with a Knife

Xie Mingyuan, a grain broker, made a lot of money last year trading foreign rice. Last winter, he returned to his home in Shengqiao, West Shanghai, and bought forty or fifty acres of land. This year, he is building a new house. When relatives and friends heard about it, they asked Xie to borrow money, but Xie refused, saying that he would not lend money without collateral. Those who wanted to borrow money were resentful. The other day, Xie went to the grave to sweep the tomb. On the way home, he was suddenly attacked from behind by an enemy who stabbed him seven or eight times in the back, neck, and legs with a knife. Xie fell to the ground unconscious. A neighbor saw him and reported it to his wife, who carried him home. Yesterday, Xie's wife applied for medical treatment and investigated the assailant, sending him to the authorities for investigation.

Concealing Red Pills in a Cotton Jacket 202

Estimated to be Over a Hundred Taels

Yesterday afternoon at about 1:00 PM, Yin Zhennan and other team members of the second team of the Water Patrol of the Municipal Public Security Bureau were patrolling the Suzhou Creek in North Shanghai when they saw a person standing on the Yuansheng tugboat. They observed that the cotton jacket he was wearing was thicker than usual and estimated that the weight of the jacket was quite different, making it suspicious. They immediately approached him for inspection and found concealed red pills estimated to be over a hundred taels inside the thick jacket. They also found five boxes of red pills in the basket he was carrying, estimated to be over ten taels. They immediately took the person and the evidence back to the South City Headquarters. During the preliminary hearing by Team Leader Xu, the person stated that his name was Yu Wenshou, 25 years old, from Huizhou. The clothes and basket were entrusted to him by a friend, and he did not know that there were prohibited items hidden inside. When asked why he was wearing the clothes if they were not his, Yu was speechless. Because the matter involved smuggling poisonous red pills, it was ordered to prepare a document and send it to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for interrogation.

Investigation of Two Cases of Seized Opium 203

Yesterday morning at approximately 3:00 AM, before dawn, Zhao Liangcai, the captain of the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau's Water Patrol Team, dispatched detectives Wang Jiheng and team member Lu Gengsheng on a patrol boat to inspect the jurisdiction. They arrived at the Huangpu Wharf in Hongkou and noticed a person standing on the dock. Shortly after, another person came from the Fengtian steamboat docked there, carrying a burlap sack onto the shore. The person appeared flustered and suspicious. The officers shouted to stop, and the person looked back, saw the police, and hastily discarded the burlap sack next to the person who was standing there, then fled. The police jumped ashore and gave chase, but quickly lost sight of the fleeing person. They returned and opened the abandoned burlap sack, discovering over 960 taels of opium inside. Suspecting the person standing nearby, they detained him and brought him and the seized opium back to the team for preliminary interrogation. The person identified himself as Zhao Liangcai, 45 years old, claiming to be a temporary dockworker. He stated that he was watching dockworkers unload cargo when someone suddenly threw a burlap sack next to him, after which the police discovered the opium and arrested him. The team was instructed to prepare a document to be submitted to the Municipal Police Bureau for investigation.

Shou Agou: Yesterday, while patrolling the Huangpu River, Zhu Desheng and other team members of the Third Squad of the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau's Water Patrol Team, Yangsi Port Police Station, observed a Shaoxing boat docked there. Upon inspecting the boat, they found an iron bucket in the cabin. After managing to open it, they discovered 23 packages of opium inside, totaling approximately 220 taels. When the police attempted to take the boat owner into custody, the owner became frightened and quickly pulled out eight silver dollars from his person, attempting to bribe the officers to avoid arrest. The officers refused the bribe and detained him, taking him, the evidence, and the bribe money back to the Third Squad. The patrol officer prepared a document and transferred it to the General Team. After a preliminary interrogation led by Team Leader Xu, the person identified himself as Shou Agou, 44 years old, from Shaoxing. He claimed that an unknown person had asked him to transport the iron bucket to Songjiang and admitted to attempting to bribe the police. He was instructed to prepare a document to be submitted to the Municipal Police Bureau for investigation.

Various Industries Telegraph Requests to Correct Business Tax 211

Cosmetics Industry: The Cosmetics Industry Association yesterday telegraphed the National Government, Executive Yuan, Ministry of Industry, and Ministry of Finance regarding the business tax issue, stating, "The implementation of the business tax on a per-industry basis means that all businesses dealing in cosmetics are taxed as cosmetics businesses, which is the duty of the people. It is reported that the business tax rates in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces classify cosmetics as the highest category, the same as paper firecrackers and funerary items, which has caused widespread dismay. We have investigated and found that the unit price of domestic cosmetic items is only a few cents, and their uses, such as toothpaste, tooth powder, and mouthwash, are for dental protection; hair oil, hair tonic, pure honey, and cold cream are for skin and hair protection; washing powder, bath salts, and prickly heat powder, as well as their accessories such as pig bristle and bone toothbrushes, rabbit hair, or silk cotton powder puffs, are designed to prevent disease and promote health, and are essential daily necessities for personal hygiene. They are not like imported cosmetics, whose unit price is over one yuan and cater to the luxurious tastes of wealthy families, or like paper firecrackers and funerary items that should be prohibited. The import of foreign cosmetics is either handled by Western medicine businesses or foreign goods businesses, so their business tax rate only needs to be paid once according to the Western medicine or foreign goods industry. We have not heard of any Chinese cosmetics manufacturers also selling foreign cosmetics, which shows that the domestic cosmetics manufacturing industry is purely operated by Chinese merchants. Therefore, their business tax rate should be taxed at a rate of 0.2% as daily necessities to ensure fairness. Otherwise, domestic cosmetics manufacturers will pay the first tax as manufacturers, then the distributors will pay the second tax as wholesalers, and then the retailers will pay the third tax as retailers. How can they compete with foreign goods? Now that the government is actively promoting domestic goods and issuing orders to encourage industry, it is necessary to protect the domestic cosmetics manufacturing industry, which is neither a luxury item nor an item to be banned like paper firecrackers and funerary items. We hereby telegraph the Executive Yuan (Ministry) to consider the situation, sympathize with the difficulties of merchants, and order (consult) the Ministry of Finance to quickly correct the business tax rate for the cosmetics industry to lighten the burden on merchants and maintain industry. We are grateful and await your decision. Cosmetics Industry Association, Shanghai, April 18, 20th year of the Republic of China."

New Medicine Industry: The New Medicine Industry Association yesterday telegraphed the Central Political Conference and the Legislative Yuan, stating, "The Ministry of Finance's revised business tax regulations for Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces tax new medicines at 0.5%, which violates the Ministry's promulgated business tax regulations. It is reported that the Ministry of Finance has submitted the revised business tax regulations to the Legislative Yuan for review. We hereby telegraph the Legislative Yuan to consider the suffering of medicine merchants and correct the new medicine business tax during the review, not exceeding 0.2% to comply with the Ministry's established guidelines and lighten the burden on merchants and citizens."

At approximately 8:00 PM the night before last, a sailboat owned by local resident Sun Jinming, carrying 31,000 bricks loaded from Xia Diti Temple in Jiashan County, was traveling to Shanghai. It had already reached the waters near the Longhua Beipiao Coal Depot when the Liheng small steamer of the Inland River Merchants Steamship Company's Shanghai-Hangzhou line, carrying passengers from Shanghai, collided head-on with the brick boat in the darkness. The company stated that it would investigate the responsibility after the Liheng steamer returned to Shanghai. Captain Chen also reported the incident to the Water Patrol Station for investigation.

He had only been there for a little over a month. This morning, he followed his master to work and got lost along the way because he did not know the route. The boy was wearing a black foreign cloth jacket, checkered homemade cloth trousers, no socks, and checkered cloth shoes. Because the address was unclear, he was temporarily sent to the Public Security Bureau for safekeeping, awaiting identification and collection.

Two Floating Corpses on the River 215

(1) A nameless male corpse suddenly floated up near the Yangjingbang Wai River a few days ago. The corpse was wearing a blue cloth long gown, had no hat, and was about thirty years old. It was discovered by a coal dreg boat, which reported it to the Water Patrol Station. The police sent a patrol to retrieve the corpse and transport it to the Rescue Bureau for collection, awaiting identification and collection. (2) Also, at 7:00 AM yesterday, a nameless male corpse floated up on the Suzhou River outside the American Consulate. The corpse was wearing an empty blue long gown and was in extremely poor condition, especially the face, which was horrifying to look at. The age was difficult to estimate, but it had probably been drowned for several months. It was discovered by Chinese patrol No. 65 of the Water Patrol Station, who retrieved it and transported it to the South City Rescue Bureau for collection.

Eye Specialist Li Yongchun from Ningbo Practices Medicine in Shanghai 216

Li Yongchun, an eye specialist from Ningbo whose family has practiced medicine for five generations, has always practiced in Ningbo. Those who have been treated by him have all been cured. Mr. Li came to Shanghai for business and was persuaded by friends to practice medicine here. He has established a clinic at No. 708, Houdeli Intersection, West Side of the Lower Sea Temple. He is offering free consultations for two weeks starting today to make a name for himself.

Yunnan Golden Fungus Transported to Shanghai for Sale 217

A certain Zhang from Yunnan has transported hundreds of pounds of golden fungus produced in his hometown to Shanghai for sale. This golden fungus is produced in the Songxue Mountains of Jiangfu, Yunnan, and has some tonic effects. It can be used as a tonic or as a vegetable. Zhang is selling the best quality fungus for two yuan per ounce and the second quality for one yuan per ounce. The Chengyu Shop and several other stores in West Xinqiao have been entrusted to sell it.

News from the Membership Department of the Young Women's Christian Association (YWCA) 218

The Membership Department of the Shanghai YWCA will hold its regular meeting for members on Tuesday, the 21st of this month, from 4:00 PM to 5:00 PM. Mr. Pan Guangdan will give a lecture on child eugenics, and there will be some games to add to the fun. All are welcome to participate. It is said that Mr. Pan is an expert in eugenics, and his lecture will surely be brilliant.

"Bell Sound" Society Established at Jiangnan College 219

The "Bell Sound" Society, organized by students of Jiangnan College, has been in preparation for three months. The inaugural meeting was held yesterday, attended by more than two hundred people, including famous scientists, faculty, staff, and students. Gu Jiwu presided over the meeting, and Cao Hanfang took notes. There were many discussions on society affairs and scientific topics, and the society's charter was approved. The meeting ended at approximately 5:00 PM.

World Book Company Offers Bargain Premiums 220

Since the World Book Company's Main Branch on Simalu began offering bargain premiums for the spring season, its newly released publications in various subjects have been selling extremely well. In particular, the three books "The Unofficial History of Chunming," "A Treasure Trove of School Administration," and "A Collection of Civil and Criminal Pleadings by Contemporary National Lawyers" have been most popular with all sectors. Other bargain books are in good condition, with some reduced to 10% of the original price. Purchases of eight dimes or more are eligible for a premium. Today is the anniversary day, and the store will be open all day.

China East Film Company Begins Filming "Huanghuagang" 221

The China East Film Company, a joint venture between a wealthy merchant from Southeast Asia and two gentlemen, Guo and Zhu, from Shanghai, has strong capital and a large scale. It has built a photography studio on Jiangwan Road, occupying a large area with perfect equipment. Recently, the company began filming the revolutionary epic "Seventy-Two Martyrs of Huanghuagang" and is recruiting male and female actors for important roles. The registration address is No. 256, intersection of Xiafei Road and Beile Road.

Disputes over Accounts Receivable in the Refining Industry 222

The refining industry in Shanghai has been greatly affected by the rising prices of raw materials and labor costs in recent years, making it difficult to sustain. As a result, prices were raised recently. Now that the end of last month's accounting period has arrived, customers in the silk and satin industry are taking a wait-and-see attitude and are unwilling to settle accounts at the higher prices. It is reported that the industry association has submitted a request to the Social Bureau for mediation to avoid escalating the dispute.

Zhengqi Daily Publishes 100th Issue Special Edition 223

The Zhengqi Daily, a tri-weekly newspaper, is publishing a special edition for its 100th issue today. The special edition is printed on high-quality red newsprint with a double-page layout. It is especially valuable because it includes the calligraphy of Sun Yat-sen and the late President Tan, as well as inscriptions by President Chiang Kai-shek, Minister Soong, and Director Pan. All news vendors in Shanghai are distributing it, and those who need to read it outside of Shanghai can contact the newspaper office at Yurenli, Yunnan Road.

News from Trade Associations 224

Incense Industry: The Incense Industry previously jointly requested the Shanghai Civic Training Association to allow them to initiate the organization of the Incense Industry Association, and nominated Zhu Xinlong, Jindingzhai, Wang Dayou, and eighteen other companies. Zhu Yongyuan, Ma Guifang, Huang Jinyi, Zhu Jiahan, Zhang Yueqing, Ye Baolin, and Sun Yaoxun were nominated as representatives. Yesterday, they received approval from the Civic Training Association to establish the association and were issued license No. 48. It is reported that the association is actively preparing and will hold its inaugural meeting soon.

Quicklime Factory Industry: The Quicklime Factory Industry Association held its 14th Executive Committee meeting yesterday, which resolved the following: (1) A letter was received from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce soliciting donations for disaster relief in Shaanxi. The committee decided to donate thirty yuan per factory and requested all group members to solicit donations separately to be collected. (2) It was reported that the Brick and Ash Industry Association's resolution accused the quicklime factories of taking advantage of the shortage of Kai Ping coal and the soaring market prices to engage in monopoly and profiteering. The committee decided that it is well known that there is a shortage of Kai Ping coal. In order to meet the needs of various factories, Fushun coal was purchased to burn ash, and prices had to be temporarily increased to maintain costs. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce has approved and recorded this. However, Zhishun, Xiehetai, Fusheng, and other brick and ash merchants from the association purchase ash from various ash factories and resell it for 2.8 to 3.8 yuan per load, making a large profit in the process. The association does not know how to maintain its reputation and dares to damage the reputation of our association. It should notify all ash factories to temporarily suspend trading with the association's merchants until they realize their mistake. At the same time, the legal consultant, Zheng, should be asked to send a warning letter. (3) The date of the association's general meeting was set for April 25th.

New Method Dyeing and Cleaning Industry: The New Method Dyeing Industry Association has appointed a committee to draft industry regulations to carry out rectification. The regulations have now been drafted and will be submitted to the competent authorities for registration after being approved by the general meeting of representatives to be held at 1:00 PM on the 25th of this month at the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce at the Tianhou Temple Bridge on North Henan Road. The association has notified all representatives to attend the meeting for discussion and asked them to submit any proposals in advance so that they can be included in the agenda. It has also requested the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the Municipal Party Department, and the Municipal Government's Social Bureau to send representatives to the meeting for guidance.

Weather Report 225

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday was: Cloudy skies, fog in the Yangtze River basin, fog and rain south of the Ma'an Islands, thunderstorms off the coast of Taiwan, easterly winds at the mouth of the Yangtze River, and gentle northerly winds in the Yellow Sea. Also, in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in Shanghai was 6.2 degrees and the lowest was 5.4 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest temperature was 81.3 degrees and the lowest was 58.6 degrees.
